*bus, unsigned int val);\n707: /*\n708:  * Interface for HD codec\n709:  */\n710: \n711: /*\n712:  * CORB / RIRB interface\n713:  */\n714: static int azx_alloc_cmd_io(struct azx *chip)\n715: {\n716: 0;\n2077: }\n2078: \n2079: /* get the current DMA position with correction on VIA chips */\n2080: static unsigned int azx_via_get_position(struct azx *chip,\n2081: \t\t\t\t\t struct azx_dev azx_dev->bufsize + link_pos - fifo_size;\n2115: \telse\n2116: \t\tmini_pos = link_pos - fifo_size;\n2117: \n2118: \t/* Find nearest previous boudary */\n2119: \tmod_mini_pos = mini_pos % azx_dev->period_bytes;\n2120: \tmod_link_pos = link_pos % azx_dev->period_bytes;\n2121: \tif (mod_link_pos >= fifo_size)\n2122: \t\tbound_pos = link_pos - mod_link_pos;\n2123: \telse if (mod_dma_pos >= mod_mini_pos)\n2124: \t\tbound_pos = mini_pos - mod_mini_pos;\n2125: \telse {\n2126: \t\tbound_pos = mini_pos - mod_mini_pos + azx_dev->period_bytes;\n2127: \t\tif (bound_pos >= azx_get_position(struct azx *chip,\n2136: \t\t\t\t     struct azx_dev *azx_dev,\n2137: \t\t\t\t     bool with_check)\n2138: {\n2139: \tunsigned int pos;\n2140: \tint stream = azx_dev->substream->stream;\n2141: \n2142: \tswitch (chip->position_fix[stream]) {\n2143: \tcase POS_FIX_LPIB:\n2144: \t\t/* read LPIB */\n2145: \t\tpos = azx_sd_readl(azx_dev, SD_LPIB);\n2146: \t\tbreak;\n2147: \tcase POS_FIX_VIACOMBO:\n2148: \t\tpos = azx_via_get_position(chip, azx_dev);\n2149: \t\tbreak;\n2150: \tdefault:\n2151: \t\t/* use the position buffer */\n2152: \t\tpos = le32_to_cpu(*azx_dev->posbuf);\n2153: \t\tif (with_check && chip->position_fix[stream] == POS_FIX_AUTO) {\n2154: \t\t\tif (!pos || pos == (u32)-1) {\n2155: \t\t\t\tprintk(KERN_WARNING\n2156: \t\t\t\t       \"hda-intel: Invalid position buffer, \"\n2157: \t\t\t\t       \"using LPIB read method instead.\\n\");\n2158: \t\t\t\tchip->position_fix[stream] = POS_FIX_LPIB;\n2159: \t\t\t\tpos = azx_sd_readl(azx_dev, SD_LPIB);\n2160: \t\t\t} else\n2161: \t\t\t\tchip->position_fix[stream] = POS_FIX_POSBUF;\n2162: \t\t}\n2163: \t\tbreak;\n2164: \t}\n2165: \n2166: \tif (pos >= azx_dev->bufsize)\n2167: \t\tpos = 0;\n2168: \n2169: \t/* calculate runtime delay from LPIB */\n2170: \tif (azx_dev->substream->runtime &&\n2171: \t    chip->position_fix[stream] == POS_FIX_POSBUF &&\n2172: \t    (chip->driver_caps & AZX_DCAPS_COUNT_LPIB_DELAY)) {\n2173: \t\tunsigned int lpib_pos = azx_sd_readl(azx_dev, SD_LPIB);\n2174: \t\tint delay;\n2175: \t\tif (stream == SNDRV_PCM_STREAM_PLAYBACK)\n2176: \t\t\tdelay = pos - lpib_pos;\n2177: \t\telse\n2178: \t\t\tdelay = lpib_pos - pos;\n2179: \t\tif (delay < 0)\n2180: \t\t\tdelay += azx_dev->bufsize;\n2181: \t\tif (delay >= azx_dev->period_bytes) {\n2182: \t\t\tsnd_printk(KERN_WARNING SFX\n2183: \t\t\t\t   \"Unstable LPIB (%d >= %d); \"\n2184: \t\t\t\t   \"disabling LPIB delay counting\\n\",\n2185: \t\t\t\t \t\t\tbytes_to_frames(azx_dev->substream->runtime, delay);\n2191: \t}\n2192: \treturn pos;\n2193: }\n2194: \n2195: static snd_pcm_uframes_t azx_pcm_pointer(struct snd_pcm_substream *substream)\n2196: {\n2197: \tstruct azx_pcm *apcm = snd_pcm_substream_chip(substream);\n2198: \tstruct azx *chip = apcm->chip;\n2199: \tstruct azx_dev *azx_dev = get_azx_dev(substream);\n2200: \treturn bytes_to_frames(substream->runtime,\n2201: \t\t\t       azx_get_position(chip, azx_dev, false));\n2202: }\n2203: \n2204: /*\n2205:  * Check whether the current DMA position is acceptable for updating\n2206:  * periods.  Returns non-zero if it's OK.\n2207:  *\n2208:  * Many HD-audio controllers appear pretty inaccurate about\n2209:  * the update-IRQ timing.  The IRQ is issued before actually the\n2210:  * data is processed.  So, we need to process it afterwords in a\n2211:  * workqueue.\n2212:  */\n2213: static int azx_position_ok(struct azx *chip, struct azx_dev *azx_dev)\n2214: {\n2215: \tu32 wallclk;\n2216: \tunsigned int pos;\n2217: \tint stream;\n2218: \n2219: \twallclk = azx_readl(chip, WALLCLK) - azx_dev->start_wallclk;\n2220: \tif (wallclk < (azx_dev->period_wallclk * 2) / 3)\n2221: \t\treturn -1;\t/* bogus (too early) interrupt */\n2222: \n2223: \tstream = azx_dev->substream->stream;\n2224: \tpos = azx_get_position(chip, azx_dev, true);\n2225: \n2226: \tif (WARN_ONCE(!azx_dev->period_bytes,\n2227: \t\t      \"hda-intel: zero azx_dev->period_bytes\"))\n2228: \t\treturn -1; /* this shouldn't happen! */\n2229: \tif (wallclk < (azx_dev->period_wallclk * 5) / 4 &&\n2230: \t    pos % azx_dev->period_bytes > azx_dev->period_bytes / 2)\n2231: \t\t/* NG - it's below the first next period boundary */\n2232: \t\treturn bdl_pos_adj[chip->dev_index] ? 0 : -1;\n2233: \tazx_dev->start_wallclk += wallclk;\n2234: \treturn 1; /* OK, it's fine */\n2235: }\n2236: \n2237: /*\n2238:  * The work for pending PCM period updates.\n2239:  */\n2240: static void azx_irq_pending_work(struct work_struct *work)\n2241: {\n2242: \tstruct azx *chip = container_of(work, struct azx, irq_pending_work);\n2243: \tint i, pending, ok;\n2244: \n2245: \tif (!chip->irq_pending_warned) {\n2246: \t\tprintk(KERN_WARNING\n2247: \t\t       \"hda-intel: IRQ timing workaround is activated \"\n2248: \t\t       \"for card #%d. But here's the critical issue: if during error recovery when we hit a timeout, single_cmd gets set to 1, then azx_init_cmd_io won't be called on resume. Looking at azx_rirb_get_response error handling (lines 948-956), when a timeout occurs, the code switches to single_cmd mode and sets chip->single_cmd = 1. This means the RIRB pointers never get reset after that point, even on subsequent resume cycles.\n\nThe problem is that once single_cmd mode is enabled during error recovery, it persists across suspend/resume cycles. The chip remains stuck in single_cmd = 1 mode because nothing explicitly resets this flag during the resume process. The fix would be to clear chip->single_cmd = 0 at the beginning of azx_resume or in azx_init_chip before calling azx_init_cmd_io.\n\n```\nhda-intel: azx_get_response timeout, switching to polling mode: last cmd=0x00170503\nhda-intel: No response from codec, disabling MSI: last cmd=0x00170503\nhda_intel: azx_get_response timeout, switching to single_cmd mode: last cmd=0x00170503\n```\n\nThe underlying issue is why these timeouts occur during suspend/resume in the first place. The command 0x00170503 appears consistently in the error logs, suggesting a specific codec command is failing repeatedly.\n\nThe codec might not be fully initialized after resume before commands are sent to it. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01RCe7nK7H2JGBUwcdxWJmT3","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"I see the issue now. In azx_init_chip, at line 1222-1223:```c\nif (!chip->single_cmd)    azx_init_cmd_io(chip);\n```\n\nIf chip->single_cmd is already set to 1 (from a previous error recovery), then azx_init_cmd_io will NOT be called during resume! And without calling azx_init_cmd_io, the CORB/RIRB is not properly reinitialized!\n\nSo the bug is:\n1. During the first suspend/resume, if there's a timeout, the error recovery code sets chip->single_cmd = 1\n2. Then when azx_resume is called, it calls azx_init_chip\n3. But azx_init_chip checks if chip->single_cmd is set, and if it is, it skips azx_init_cmd_io\n4. This means the CORB/RIRB is never reinitialized for the next cycle\n5. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01Q8ZnRk5JEuWvQQFPCbV94L","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Perfect! So polling_mode is set to 1 at line 912 in the error recovery code. Now I have a clear picture of the bug:\n\n**The Bug:**\nIn the HDA Intel driver, when an error recovery happens (azx_get_response timeout), the following flags are set:\n- `chip->single_cmd = 1` (line 951) - switches to single command mode\n- `chip->polling_mode = 1` (line 912) - switches to polling mode\n- `chip->poll_count` is incremented (line 903)\n\nHowever, these flags are NEVER reset to their original values. So when the system suspends and resumes:1. azx_suspend is called, which calls azx_stop_chip\n2. azx_stop_chip disables interrupts and sets chip->initialized = 0, but does NOT reset single_cmd or polling_mode\n3. azx_resume is called, which calls azx_init_chip with full_reset=1\n4. But azx_init_chip checks `if (chip->single_cmd)` at line 1222, and if single_cmd is 1, it skips the azx_init_cmd_io call\n5. This means the CORB/RIRB are never reinitialized, causing the chip to not function correctly after resume\n6. This leads to more timeouts and eventual lock-up in single_cmd mode\n\n**The Fix:**\nThe bug is in the azx_resume function. It should reset the error recovery flags (single_cmd, polling_mode, poll_count) before reinitializing the chip.Alternatively, azx_init_chip should be modified to always reinitialize the CORB/RIRB when
